   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiceless velar fricative
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">

         </div>

       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiceless velar fricative
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in some
       <a href="/wiki/Speech" title="Speech">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . It was part of the consonant inventory of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_English_language" title="Old English language">
        Old English
       </a>
       and can still be found in some dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , most notably in
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">
        Scottish English
       </a>
       , e.g. in
       <i>
        loch
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        broch
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        saugh
       </i>
       (willow).
      </p>
      <p>
       The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents this sound is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        x
       </span>
       ⟩, the
       <a href="/wiki/X" title="X">
        Latin and English letter x
       </a>
       . It is also used in
       <a href="/wiki/Phonetic_transcription#Narrow_versus_broad_transcription" title="Phonetic transcription">
        broad transcription
       </a>
       instead of the symbol ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        χ
       </span>
       ⟩, the
       <a href="/wiki/Chi_(letter)#Greek_chi" title="Chi (letter)">
        Greek chi
       </a>
       , (or, more properly, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ꭓ
       </span>
       ⟩, the
       <a href="/wiki/Chi_(letter)#Latin_chi" title="Chi (letter)">
        Latin chi
       </a>
       ) for the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">
        voiceless uvular fricative
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also a
       <b>
        voiceless post-velar fricative
       </b>
       (also called
       <b>
        pre-uvular
       </b>
       ) in some languages. For
       <b>
        voiceless pre-velar fricative
       </b>
       (also called
       <b>
        post-palatal
       </b>
       ), see
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless palatal fricative">
        voiceless palatal fricative
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_velar_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiceless velar fricative:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
         fricative
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by constricting air flow through a narrow channel at the place of articulation, causing
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulence
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">
         velar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the back of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue" title="Tongue">
         tongue
        </a>
        (the dorsum) at the
        <a href="/wiki/Soft_palate" title="Soft palate">
         soft palate
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size:24px">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          xʲʼ
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         ejective palatalised
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence">
        Occurrence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_velar_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Occurrence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The voiceless velar fricative and its labialized variety are traditionally postulated to have occurred in
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">
        Proto-Germanic
       </a>
       , the ancestor of the
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic languages
       </a>
       , as the
       <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_reconstruction" title="Linguistic reconstruction">
        reflex
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">
        Proto-Indo-European
       </a>
       voiceless palatal and velar stops and the labialized voiceless velar stop. Thus Proto-Indo-European *
       <b>
        ḱ
       </b>
       r̥nom "horn" and *
       <b>
        kʷ
       </b>
       ód "what" became Proto-Germanic *
       <b>
        h
       </b>
       urnan and *
       <b>
        hw
       </b>
       at, where *h and *hw were likely to be
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [x]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [xʷ]
       </span>
       . This
       <a href="/wiki/Sound_change" title="Sound change">
        sound change
       </a>
       is part of
       <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">
        Grimm's law
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek" title="Modern Greek">
        Modern Greek
       </a>
       , the voiceless velar fricative (with its
       <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">
        allophone
       </a>
       the voiceless palatal fricative
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_fricative#Palatal" title="Voiceless palatal fricative">
         ç
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       , occurring before front vowels) originated from the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">
        Ancient Greek
       </a>
       voiceless aspirated stop
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /kʰ/
       </span>
       in a sound change that
       <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">
        lenited
       </a>
       Greek aspirated stops into fricatives.
      </p>

        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Urban_East_Norwegian" title="Urban East Norwegian">
          Urban East
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVanvik197940_16-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVanvik197940-16">
           [16]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="no">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_alphabet" title="Norwegian alphabet">
            <b>
             h
            </b>
            at
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [xɑːt]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'hate'
        </td>
        <td>
         Possible allophone of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /h/
         </span>
         near back vowels; can be voiced
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">
           ɣ
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         between two voiced sounds.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVanvik197940_16-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVanvik197940-16">
           [16]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_phonology" title="Norwegian phonology">
          Norwegian phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

          Vietnamese phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">

         </a>

        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="fy">
           tú
           <b>
            ch
           </b>
          </span>
         </i>

        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [tyx]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'dust'
        </td>
        <td>
         Allophone of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /χ/
         </span>
         , only occurring after
         <a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">
          close vowels
         </a>
         (
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [i]
         </span>
         ,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [y]
         </span>
         and
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [u]
         </span>
         )
        </td>
